This Command Does\n    10→\n    11→1. **Scaffold Interfaces** - Define types/interfaces first\n    12→2. **Generate Tests First** - Write failing tests (RED)\n    13→3. **Implement Minimal Code** - Write just enough to pass (GREEN)\n    14→4. **Refactor** - Improve code while keeping tests green (REFACTOR)\n    15→5. **Verify Coverage** - Ensure 80%+ test coverage\n    16→\n    17→## When to Use\n    18→\n    19→Use `/tdd` when:\n    20→- Implementing new features\n    21→- Adding new functions/components\n    22→- Fixing bugs (write test that reproduces bug first)\n    23→- Refactoring existing code\n    24→- Building critical business logic\n    25→\n    26→## How It Works\n    27→\n    28→The tdd-guide agent will:\n    29→\n    30→1. **Define interfaces** for inputs/outputs\n    31→2. **Write tests that will FAIL** (because code doesn't exist yet)\n    32→3. **Run tests** and verify they fail for the right reason\n    33→4. **Write minimal implementation** to make tests pass\n    34→5. **Run tests** and verify they pass\n    35→6. **Refactor** code while keeping tests green\n    36→7. **Check coverage** and add more tests if below 80%\n    37→\n    38→## TDD Cycle\n    39→\n    40→```\n    41→RED → GREEN → REFACTOR → REPEAT\n    42→\n    43→RED:      Write a failing test\n    44→GREEN:    Write minimal code to pass\n    45→REFACTOR: Improve code, keep tests passing\n    46→REPEAT:   Next feature/scenario\n    47→```\n    48→\n    49→## Example Usage\n    50→\n    51→```\n    52→User: /tdd I need a function to calculate market liquidity score\n    53→\n Ready to implement.\n   137→\n   138→## Step 4: Implement Minimal Code (GREEN)\n   139→\n   140→```typescript\n   141→// lib/liquidity.ts\n   142→export function calculateLiquidityScore(market: MarketData): number {\n   143→  // Handle zero volume edge case\n   144→  if (market.totalVolume === 0) {\n   145→    return 0\n   146→  }\n   147→\n   148→  // Calculate component scores (0-100 scale)\n   149→  const volumeScore = Math.min(market.totalVolume / 1000, 100)\n   150→  const spreadScore = Math.max(100 - (market.bidAskSpread * 1000), 0)\n   151→  const traderScore = Math.min(market.activeTraders / 10, 100)\n   152→\n   153→  // Recent activity bonus\n   154→  const hoursSinceLastTrade = (Date.now() - market.lastTradeTime.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60)\n   155→  const recencyScore = Math.max(100 - (hoursSinceLastTrade * 10), 0)\n   156→\n   157→  // Weighted average\n   158→  const score = (\n   159→    volumeScore * 0.4 +\n   160→    spreadScore * 0.3 +\n   161→    traderScore * 0.2 +\n   162→    recencyScore * 0.1\n   163→  )\n   164→\n   165→  return Math.min(Math.max(score, 0), 100) // Clamp to 0-100\n   166→}\n   167→```\n   168→\n   169→## Step 5: Run Tests - Verify PASS\n   170→\n   171→```bash\n   172→npm test lib/liquidity.test.ts\n   173→\n   174→PASS lib/liquidity.test.ts\n   175→  ✓ should return high score for liquid market (3 ms)\n   176→  ✓ should return low score for illiquid market (2 ms)\n   177→  ✓ should handle edge case: zero volume (1 ms)\n   178→\n   179→3 tests passed\n   180→```\n   181→\n   182→✅ All tests passing!\n   183→\n   184→## Step 6: Refactor (IMPROVE)\n   185→\n   186→```typescript\n   187→// lib/liquidity.ts - Refactored with constants and better readability\n   188→const WEIGHTS = {\n   189→  VOLUME: 0.4,\n   190→  SPREAD: 0.3,\n   191→  TRADERS: 0.2,\n   192→  RECENCY: 0.1,\n   193→} as const\n   194→\n   195→const SCALE_FACTORS = {\n   196→  VOLUME: 1000,\n   197→  SPREAD: 1000,\n   198→  TRADERS: 10,\n   199→  RECENCY_PENALTY: 10,\n   200→} as const\n   201→\n   202→function clamp(value: number, min: number, max: number): number {\n   203→  return Math.min(Math.max(value, min), max)\n   204→}\n   205→\n   206→export function calculateLiquidityScore(market: MarketData): number {\n   207→  if (market.totalVolume === 0) return 0\n   208→\n   209→  const volumeScore = Math.min(market.totalVolume / SCALE_FACTORS.VOLUME, 100)\n   210→  const spreadScore = clamp(100 - (market.bidAskSpread * SCALE_FACTORS.SPREAD), 0, 100)\n   211→  const traderScore = Math.min(market.activeTraders / SCALE_FACTORS.TRADERS, 100)\n   212→\n   213→  const hoursSinceLastTrade = (Date.now() - market.lastTradeTime.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60)\n   214→  const recencyScore = clamp(100 - (hoursSinceLastTrade * SCALE_FACTORS.RECENCY_PENALTY), 0, 100)\n   215→\n   216→  const weightedScore =\n   217→    volumeScore * WEIGHTS.VOLUME +\n   218→    spreadScore * WEIGHTS.SPREAD +\n   219→    traderScore * WEIGHTS.TRADERS +\n   220→    recencyScore * WEIGHTS.RECENCY\n   221→\n   222→  return clamp(weightedScore, 0, 100)\n   223→}\n   224→```\n   225→\n   226→## Step 7: Verify Tests Still Pass\n   227→\n   228→```bash\n   229→npm test lib/liquidity.test.ts\n   230→\n   231→PASS lib/liquidity.test.ts\n   232→  ✓ should return high score for liquid market (3 ms)\n   233→  ✓ should return low score for illiquid market (2 ms)\n   234→  ✓ should handle edge case: zero volume (1 ms)\n   235→\n   236→3 tests passed\n   237→```\n   238→\n   239→✅ Refactoring complete, tests still passing!\n   240→\n   241→## Step 8: Check Coverage\n   242→\n   243→```bash\n   244→npm test -- --coverage lib/liquidity.test.ts\n   245→\n   246→File           | % Stmts | % 80%)\n   251→```\n   252→\n   253→✅ TDD session complete!\n   254→```\n   255→\n   256→## TDD Best Practices\n   257→\n   258→**DO:**\n   259→- ✅ Write the test FIRST, before any implementation\n   260→- ✅ Run tests and verify they FAIL before implementing\n   261→- ✅ Write minimal code to make tests pass\n   262→- ✅ Refactor only after tests are green\n   263→- ✅ Add edge cases and error scenarios\n   264→- ✅ Aim for 80%+ coverage (100% for critical code)\n   265→\n   266→**DON'T:**\n   267→- ❌ Write implementation before tests\n   268→- ❌ Skip running tests after each change\n   269→- ❌ Write too much code at once\n   270→- ❌ Ignore failing tests\n   271→- ❌ Test implementation details (test behavior)\n   272→- ❌ Mock everything (prefer integration tests)\n   273→\n   274→## Test Types to Include\n   275→\n   276→**Unit Tests** (Function-level):\n   277→- Happy path scenarios\n   278→- Edge cases (empty, null, max values)\n   279→- Error conditions\n   280→- Boundary values\n   281→\n   282→**Integration Tests** (Component-level):\n   283→- API endpoints\n   284→- Database operations\n   285→- External service calls\n   286→- React components with hooks\n   287→\n   288→**E2E Tests** (use `/e2e` command):\n   289→- Critical user flows\n   290→- Multi-step processes\n   291→- Full stack integration\n   292→\n   293→## Coverage Requirements\n   294→\n   295→- **80% minimum** for all code\n   296→- **100% required** for:\n   297→  - Financial calculations\n   298→  - Authentication logic\n   299→  - Security-critical code\n   300→  - Core business logic\n   301→\n   302→## Important Notes\n   303→\n   304→**MANDATORY**: Tests must be written BEFORE implementation. The TDD cycle is:\n   305→\n   306→1. **RED** - Write failing test\n   307→2. **GREEN** - Implement to pass\n   308→3. **REFACTOR** - Improve code\n   309→\n   310→Never skip the RED phase. Creates test journeys, runs tests, captures screenshots/videos/traces, and uploads artifacts.\n     3→---\n     4→\n     5→# E2E Command\n     6→\n     7→This command invokes the **e2e-runner** agent to generate, maintain, and execute end-to-end tests using Playwright.\n     8→\n     9→## What This Command Does\n    10→\n    11→1. **Generate Test Journeys** - Create Playwright tests for user flows\n    12→2. **Run E2E Tests** - Execute tests across browsers\n    13→3. **Capture Artifacts** - Screenshots, videos, traces on failures\n    14→4. **Upload Results** - HTML reports and JUnit XML\n    15→5. **Identify Flaky Tests** - Quarantine unstable tests\n    16→\n    17→## When to Use\n    18→\n    19→Use `/e2e` when:\n    20→- Testing critical user journeys (login, trading, payments)\n    21→- Verifying multi-step flows work end-to-end\n    22→- Testing UI interactions and navigation\n    23→- Validating integration between frontend and backend\n    24→- Preparing for production deployment\n    25→\n    26→## How It Works\n    27→\n    28→The e2e-runner agent will:\n    29→\n    30→1. **Analyze user flow** and identify test scenarios\n    31→2. **Generate Playwright test** using Page Object Model pattern\n    32→3. **Run tests** across multiple browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Safari)\n    33→4. **Capture failures** with screenshots, videos, and traces\n    34→5. **Generate report** with results and artifacts\n    35→6. **Identify flaky tests** and recommend fixes\n    36→\n    37→## Example Usage\n    38→\n    39→```\n    40→User: /e2e Test the market search and view flow\n    41→\n    42→Agent (e2e-runner):\n    43→# E2E Test Generation: Market Search and View Flow\n    44→\n    45→## Test Scenario Identified\n    46→\n    47→**User Journey:** Market Search → View Results → Click Market → View Details\n    48→\n    49→**Test Coverage:**\n    50→1. Navigate to markets page\n    51→2. Perform semantic search\n    52→3. Verify search results\n    53→4. Click on first result\n    54→5. Verify market details page loads\n    55→6. Verify chart renders\n    56→\n    57→## Generated Test Code\n    58→\n    59→```typescript\n    60→// tests/e2e/markets/search-and-view.spec.ts\n    61→import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test'\n    62→import { MarketsPage } from '../../pages/MarketsPage'\n    63→import { MarketDetailsPage } from '../../pages/MarketDetailsPage'\n    64→\n    65→test.describe('Market Search and View Flow', () => {\n    66→  test('user can search markets and view details', async ({ page }) => {\n    67→    // 1. Navigate to markets page\n    68→    const marketsPage = new MarketsPage(page)\n    69→    await marketsPage.goto()\n    70→\n    71→    // Verify page loaded\n    72→    await expect(page).toHaveTitle(/Markets/)\n    73→    await expect(page.locator('h1')).toContainText('Markets')\n    74→\n    75→    // 2. Perform semantic search\n    76→    await marketsPage.searchMarkets('election')\n    77→\n    78→    // Wait for API response\n    79→    await page.waitForResponse(resp =>\n    80→      resp.url().includes('/api/markets/search') && resp.status() === 200\n    81→    )\n    82→\n    83→    // 3. Verify search results\n    84→    const marketCards = marketsPage.marketCards\n    85→    await expect(marketCards.first()).toBeVisible()\n    86→    const resultCount = await marketCards.count()\n    87→    expect(resultCount).toBeGreaterThan(0)\n    88→\n    89→    // Take screenshot of search results\n    90→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'artifacts/search-results.png' })\n    91→\n    92→    // 4. Click on first result\n    93→    const firstMarketTitle = await marketCards.first().textContent()\n    94→    await marketCards.first().click()\n    95→\n    96→    // 5. Verify market details page loads\n    97→    await expect(page).toHaveURL(/\\/markets\\/[a-z0-9-]+/)\n    98→\n    99→    const detailsPage = new MarketDetailsPage(page)\n   100→    await expect(detailsPage.marketName).toBeVisible()\n   101→    await expect(detailsPage.marketDescription).toBeVisible()\n   102→\n   103→    // 6. Verify chart renders\n   104→    await expect(detailsPage.priceChart).toBeVisible()\n   105→\n   106→    // Verify market name matches\n   107→    const detailsTitle = await detailsPage.marketName.textContent()\n   108→    expect(detailsTitle?.toLowerCase()).toContain(\n   109→      firstMarketTitle?.toLowerCase().substring(0, 20) || ''\n   110→    )\n   111→\n   112→    // Take screenshot of market details\n   113→    await page.screenshot({ path: 'artifacts/market-details.png' })\n   114→  })\n   115→\n   116→  test('search with no results shows empty state', async ({ page }) => {\n   117→    const marketsPage = new MarketsPage(page)\n   118→    await marketsPage.goto()\n   119→\n   120→    // Search for non-existent market\n   121→    await marketsPage.searchMarkets('xyznonexistentmarket123456')\n   122→\n   123→    // Verify empty state\n   124→    await expect(page.locator('[data-testid=\"no-results\"]')).toBeVisible()\n   125→    await expect(page.locator('[data-testid=\"no-results\"]')).toContainText(\n   126→      /no.*results|no.*markets/i\n   127→    )\n   128→\n   129→    const marketCount = await marketsPage.marketCards.count()\n   130→    expect(marketCount).toBe(0)\n   131→  })\n   132→\n   133→  test('can clear search and see all markets again', async ({ page }) => {\n   134→    const marketsPage = new MarketsPage(page)\n   135→    await marketsPage.goto()\n   136→\n   137→    // Initial market count\n   138→    const initialCount = await marketsPage.marketCards.count()\n   139→\n   140→    // Perform search\n   141→    await marketsPage.searchMarkets('trump')\n   142→    await page.waitForLoadState('networkidle')\n   143→\n   144→    // Verify filtered results\n   145→    const filteredCount = await marketsPage.marketCards.count()\n   146→    expect(filteredCount).toBeLessThan(initialCount)\n   147→\n   148→    // Clear search\n   149→    await marketsPage.searchInput.clear()\n   150→    await page.waitForLoadState('networkidle')\n   151→\n   152→    // Verify all markets shown again\n   153→    const finalCount = await marketsPage.marketCards.count()\n   154→    expect(finalCount).toBe(initialCount)\n   155→  })\n   156→})\n   157→```\n   158→\n   159→## Running Tests\n   160→\n   161→```bash\n   162→# Run the generated test\n   163→npx playwright test tests/e2e/markets/search-and-view.spec.ts\n   164→\n   165→Running 3 tests using 3 workers\n   166→\n   167→  ✓  [chromium] › search-and-view.spec.ts:5:3 › user can search markets and view details (4.2s)\n   168→  ✓  [chromium] › search-and-view.spec.ts:52:3 › search with no results shows empty state (1.8s)\n   169→  ✓  [chromium] › search-and-view.spec.ts:67:3 › can clear search and see all markets again (2.9s)\n   170→\n   171→  3 passed (9.1s)\n   172→\n   173→Artifacts generated:\n   174→- artifacts/search-results.png\n   175→- artifacts/market-details.png\n   176→- playwright-report/index.html\n   177→```\n   178→\n   179→## Test Report\n   180→\n   181→```\n the following artifacts are captured:\n   208→\n   209→**On All Tests:**\n   210→- HTML Report with timeline and results\n   211→- JUnit XML for CI integration\n   212→\n   213→**On Failure Only:**\n   214→- Screenshot of the failing state\n   215→- Video recording of the test\n   216→- Trace file for debugging (step-by-step replay)\n   217→- Network logs\n   218→- Console logs\n   219→\n   220→## Viewing Artifacts\n   221→\n   222→```bash\n   223→# View HTML report in browser\n   224→npx playwright show-report\n   225→\n   226→# View specific trace file\n   227→npx playwright show-trace artifacts/trace-abc123.zip\n   228→\n   229→# Screenshots are saved in artifacts/ directory\n   230→open artifacts/search-results.png\n   231→```\n   232→\n   233→## Flaky Test Detection\n   234→\n   235→If a test fails intermittently:\n   236→\n   237→```\n   238→⚠️  FLAKY TEST DETECTED: tests/e2e/markets/trade.spec.ts\n   239→\n   240→Test passed 7/10 runs (70% pass rate)\n   241→\n   242→Common Verify element is not hidden by animation\n   250→\n   251→Quarantine recommendation: Mark as test.fixme() until fixed\n   252→```\n   253→\n   254→## Browser Configuration\n   255→\n   256→Tests run on multiple browsers by default:\n   257→- ✅ Chromium (Desktop Chrome)\n   258→- ✅ Firefox (Desktop)\n   259→- ✅ WebKit (Desktop Safari)\n   260→- ✅ Mobile Chrome (optional)\n   261→\n   262→Configure in `playwright.config.ts` to adjust browsers.\n   263→\n   264→## CI/CD Integration\n   265→\n   266→Add to your CI pipeline:\n   267→\n   268→```yaml\n   269→# .github/workflows/e2e.yml\n   270→- name: Install Playwright\n   271→  run: npx playwright install --with-deps\n   272→\n   273→- name: Run E2E tests\n   274→  run: npx playwright test\n   275→\n   276→- name: Upload artifacts\n   277→  if: always()\n   278→  uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3\n   279→  with:\n   280→    name: playwright-report\n   281→    path: playwright-report/\n   282→```\n   283→\n   284→## PMX-Specific Critical Flows\n   285→\n   286→For PMX, prioritize these E2E tests:\n   287→\n   288→**🔴 CRITICAL (Must Always Pass):**\n   289→1. \\\n    56→    jq 'map(.messages) | flatten | length'\n    57→fi\n    58→\n    59→# Java\n    60→if [ -f \"pom.xml\" ] || [ -f \"build.gradle\" ]; then\n    61→  echo \"Run: mvn spotbugs:check   85→### Additional Pattern Check\n    86→\n    87→```bash\n    88→# Direct grep for common secret patterns (fallback if gitleaks not installed)\n    89→echo \"=== Manual Secret Patterns ===\"\n    90→grep -rn \\\n    91→  -E '(password|passwd|secret|api_key|apikey|token|auth_token|access_token|private_key)\\s*=\\s*[\"\\x27][^\"\\x27]{8,}' \\\n    92→ .Results[] |\n   117→    select(.Vulnerabilities != null) |\n   118→    {\n   119→      target: .Target,\n   120→      critical: [.Vulnerabilities[] | select(.Severity == \"CRITICAL\")] | length,\n 169→  # Scan Dockerfile for misconfigurations\n   170→  trivy config Dockerfile \\\n   171→    --severity HIGH,CRITICAL \\\n   172→    --exit-code 0 2>/dev/null | head -40\n   173→\n   174→  # Check root\\|^RUN.*sudo\\|^RUN.*chmod 777\" \"$DOCKERFILE\" && \\\n   178→    echo \"WARNING: Root execution or broad permissions detected\" || echo \"OK: No root user issues\"\n   179→  grep -qn \"^USER \" \"$DOCKERFILE\" && echo \"OK: Non-root USER defined\" || \\\n   180→    echo \"WARNING: No USER instruction — container runs as root\"\n   181→  grep -qn \"COPY \\.\\.\" \"$DOCKERFILE\" && echo \"WARNING: Copying entire context\" || true\n   182→\n   183→  # Scan built image (if available)\n   184→  if docker image inspect \"$IMAGE_TAG\" &>/dev/null; then\n   185→    trivy image \"$IMAGE_TAG\" \\\n   186→      --severity HIGH,CRITICAL \\\n   187→      --exit-code 0 \\\n   188→      --format json \\\n   189→      --output trivy-image-results.json\n   190→\n   191→    jq '\n   192→      .Results[] |\n   193→      select(.Vulnerabilities != null) |\n   194→      {\n   195→        target: .Target,\n   196→        critical_cves: [.Vulnerabilities[] | select(.Severity == \"CRITICAL\") | .VulnerabilityID],\n   197→        high_count: [.Vulnerabilities[] | select(.Severity == \"HIGH\")] | length\n   198→      }\n   199→    ' trivy-image-results.json\n   200→  fi\n   201→fi\n   202→```\n   203→\n   204→---\n   205→\n   206→## Step 5: DAST — Dynamic Analysis (Optional)\n   207→\n   208→Only run if a local app URL is provided or a docker-compose environment is (yes/no/security-only)\n   136→```\n   137→\n   138→For `check` (CI mode): output machine-readable JSON, exit 1 if CRITICAL or HIGH vulnerabilities found.\n   139→\n   140→### 6. Apply Upgrades\n   141→\n   142→**Patch only (safe, apply automatically):**\n   143→```bash\n   144→# pnpm\n   145→pnpm update              # updates within semver range in package.json\n   146→\n   147→# npm\n   148→npm update\n   149→\n   150→# poetry\n   151→poetry update\n   152→\n   153→# go mod\n   154→go get -u=patch ./...\n   155→go mod tidy\n   156→```\n   157→\n   158→**Security fix (specific package):**\n   159→```bash\n   160→# pnpm\n   161→pnpm add lodash@latest\n   162→\n   163→# npm\n   164→npm install lodash@latest\n   165→\n   166→# go\n   167→go get golang.org/x/net@latest\n   168→go mod tidy\n   169→```\n   170→\n   171→**Minor upgrades (one by one, interactive):**\n   172→For each minor upgrade: show the changelog URL, ask to proceed, apply, run tests.\n   173→\n   174→```bash\n   175→# Use interactive mode\n   176→pnpm update --interactive\n   177→# or\n   178→npx npm-check-updates --interactive\n   179→```\n   180→\n   181→**Major upgrades — always manual:**\n   182→- Show migration guide URL\n   183→- Do NOT auto-apply\n   184→- Instruct: \"Review migration guide, then: pnpm add <package>@latest\"\n   185→\n   186→### 7. {"parentUuid":"1d1c2960-9a86-4f4f-9efb-c36b01dd72b3","isSidechain":true,"userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/marvinrichter/Work/everything-claude-code","sessionId":"975742db-ffef-4d1f-b820-6a97017721c6","version":"2.1.71","gitBranch":"main","agentId":"a1ab3b78aeb29acca","slug":"adaptive-wandering-music","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UyZFk1n3xGDjE986xfN1BY","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: evolve\n     3→description: Cluster accumulated instincts into skills, commands, or agents — runs conflict detection first, groups instincts by trigger domain, scores clusters by confidence, and writes evolved files with --generate.\n     4→command: true\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→# Evolve Command\n     8→\n     9→## Implementation\n    10→\n    11→Run the instinct CLI using the plugin root path:\n    12→\n    13→```bash\n    14→python3 \"${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/skills/continuous-learning-v2/scripts/instinct-cli.py\" evolve [--generate]\n    15→```\n    16→\n    17→Or if `CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT` is not set (manual installation):\n    18→\n    19→```bash\n    20→python3 ~/.claude/skills/continuous-learning-v2/scripts/instinct-cli.py evolve [--generate]\n    21→```\n    22→\n    23→Analyzes instincts and clusters related ones into higher-level structures:\n    24→- **Commands**: When instincts describe user-invoked actions\n    25→- **Skills**: When instincts describe auto-triggered behaviors\n    26→- **Agents**: When instincts describe complex, multi-step processes\n    27→\n    28→## Usage\n    29→\n    30→```\n    31→/evolve                    # Analyze all instincts and suggest evolutions\n    32→/evolve --generate         # Also generate files under evolved/{skills,commands,agents}\n    33→```\n    34→\n    35→## Evolution Rules\n    36→\n    37→### → Command (User-Invoked)\n    38→When instincts describe actions a user would explicitly request:\n    39→- Multiple instincts about \"when user asks to...\"\n    40→- Instincts with triggers like \"when creating a new X\"\n    41→- Instincts that follow a repeatable sequence\n    42→\n    43→Example:\n    44→- `new-table-step1`: \"when adding a database table, create migration\"\n    45→- `new-table-step2`: \"when adding a database table, update schema\"\n    46→- `new-table-step3`: \"when adding a database table, regenerate types\"\n    47→\n    48→→ Creates: **new-table** command\n    49→\n    50→### → Skill (Auto-Triggered)\n    51→When instincts describe behaviors that should happen automatically:\n    52→- Pattern-matching triggers\n    53→- Error handling responses\n    54→- Code style enforcement\n    55→\n    56→Example:\n    57→- `prefer-functional`: \"when writing functions, prefer functional style\"\n    58→- `use-immutable`: \"when modifying state, use immutable patterns\"\n    59→- `avoid-classes`: \"when designing modules, avoid class-based design\"\n    60→\n    61→→ Creates: `functional-patterns` skill\n    62→\n    63→### → Agent (Needs Depth/Isolation)\n    64→When instincts describe complex, multi-step processes that benefit from isolation:\n    65→- Debugging workflows\n    66→- Refactoring sequences\n    67→- Research tasks\n    68→\n    69→Example:\n    70→- `debug-step1`: \"when debugging, first check logs\"\n    71→- `debug-step2`: \"when debugging, isolate the failing component\"\n    72→- `debug-step3`: \"when debugging, create minimal reproduction\"\n    73→- `debug-step4`: \"when debugging, verify fix with test\"\n    74→\n    75→→ Creates: **debugger** agent\n    76→\n    77→## Conflict Resolution (Run First)\n    78→\n    79→Before evolving, check and resolve conflicts:\n    80→\n    81→```bash\n    82→python3 \"${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/skills/continuous-learning-v2/scripts/conflict-detector.py\"\n    83→```\n    84→\n    85→If conflicts exist in `~/.claude/homunculus/conflicts.json`, resolve them before evolving:\n    86→- Show each conflict pair with their confidence scores\n    87→- Recommend keeping the higher-confidence instinct\n    88→- User can run `--fix` to auto-resolve (removes lower-confidence instinct)\n    89→- Only proceed to evolution after conflicts are resolved or acknowledged\n    90→\n    91→## What to Do\n    92→\n    93→1. Run conflict detection first (see above)\n    94→2. Detect current project context\n    95→2. Read project + global instincts (project takes precedence on ID conflicts)\n    96→3. Render ranked output (see format below)\n    43→5. Show removal candidates if any\n    44→\n    45→## Output Format\n    46→\n    47→```\n    48→============================================================\n    49→  INSTINCT REPORT — 14 total (project: my-app + 4 global)\n    50→  Updated: 2026-03-09\n    51→============================================================\n    52→\n    53→TOP CONFIDENCE (10 highest)\n    54→  #1  ████████████  89%  ↑  validate-user-input     [global]  security\n    55→  #2  ███████████░  85%  →  test-first-workflow     [project] testing     +8/-1/2\n    56→  #3  ███████████░  84%  ↑  grep-before-edit        [project] workflow    +6/-0/1\n    57→  #4  ██████████░░  82%  →  immutable-state         [project] patterns    +5/-0/0\n    58→  #5  █████████░░░  78%  ↓  async-over-sync         [project] patterns    +2/-3/1\n    59→  ...\n    60→\n    61→LOW CONFIDENCE — candidates for removal (confidence ≤ 20% or unused > 90 days)\n    62→  ○  lint-before-commit   15%  ↓  [project] unused 112 days — consider removing\n    63→  ○  manual-testing-ok    18%  ↓  [project] unused 95 days  — consider removing\n    64→\n    65→DECAY STATUS\n    66→  Instincts unused 30+ days:  3\n    67→  Instincts unused 90+ days:  2 (flagged)\n    68→  Archived this week:         0\n    69→\n    70→Run /instinct-outcome <id> good|bad|neutral to record outcomes.\n    71→Run /evolve to cluster high-confidence instincts into skills/commands.\n    72→```\n    73→\n    74→## Trend Calculation\n    75→\n    76→For each instinct, look up its entries in `~/.claude/homunculus/outcomes.jsonl`:\n    77→\n    78→```js\n    79→// Filter last 3 outcomes for this instinct\n    80→const recent = allOutcomes\n    81→  .filter(o => o.instinct_id === id)\n    82→  .slice(-3);\n    83→\n    84→const avgDelta = recent.length === 0 ? 0\n    85→  : recent.reduce((sum, o) => sum + (o.confidence_after - o.confidence_before), 0) / recent.length;\n    86→\n    87→const trend = avgDelta > 0.03 ? '↑' : avgDelta < -0.03 ? '↓' : '→';\n    88→```\n    89→\n    90→## Confidence Bar Rendering\n    91→\n    92→Use block characters to render a 12-cell bar:\n    93→- Filled cells: `Math.round(confidence * 12)`\n    94→- Use `█` for filled, `░` for empty\n    95→\n    96→## Notes\n    97→\n    98→- Outcome counts format: `+good/-bad/neutral`\n    99→- Instincts below 20% confidence should be surfaced for manual review\n   100→- Never auto-delete — only surface for user decision\n   101→- Link to `/instinct-outcome` for recording new outcomes\n   102→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Recommended with `/overnight`:\n    42→1. All steps from Components Mode\n    43→2. **prompt-quality-scorer `--all`** → prompt engineering quality\n    44→3. **learning-audit** → continuous-learning-v2 health\n    45→4. **workflow-check** → 6 critical developer journey coverage\n    46→5. **competitive-review** → clarc vs. competitors feature matrix\n    47→6. **agent-system-reviewer** → synthesizes everything into a unified Priority Matrix\n    48→\n    49→**Use**: Monthly, before major roadmap planning sessions.\n    50→\n    51→## Steps Claude Should Follow\n    52→\n    53→### For Quick Mode\n    54→\n    55→1.        → implementation breakdown\n    84→```\n    85→\n    86→---\n    87→\n    88→## Path E — Understand clarc\n    89→\n    90→**The 10 most-used commands:**\n    91→\n    92→| Command | What it Creates a structured incident document, guides root cause analysis, generates status page updates and Slack messages, and sets up a post-mortem after resolution.\n     3→---\n     4→\n     5→# Incident\n     6→\n     7→Open a production incident, guide the response, and generate all communication artifacts.\n     8→\n     9→## Instructions\n    10→\n    11→### 1. Parse Arguments\n    12→\n    13→`$ARGUMENTS` can be:\n    14→- Description of what's broken: `checkout failing with 500 errors`\n    15→- Severity override: `P0 checkout down`\n    16→- `post-mortem <incident-file>`: write post-mortem for a resolved incident\n    17→- `runbook <service> <failure>`: generate a runbook\n    18→\n    19→If empty: ask \"What's broken? Describe the symptoms.\"\n    20→\n    21→### 2. Assess Severity\n    22→\n    23→Based on the description, determine severity:\n    24→- P0: complete outage, login broken, payments failing, data loss\n    25→- P1: major feature broken for many users\n    26→- P2: degraded performance or minor feature broken\n    27→- P3: cosmetic, workaround exists\n    28→\n    29→Ask for confirmation if uncertain: \"Based on the description, this looks like P1. Correct?\"\n    30→\n    31→### 3. Create Incident Document\n    32→\n    33→Create `docs/incidents/YYYY-MM-DD-HH-MM-<short-name>.md`:\n    34→\n    35→```markdown\n    36→# Incident: <Description>\n    37→\n    38→**Date:** YYYY-MM-DD\n    39→**Time:** HH:MM UTC\n    40→**Severity:** P<N>\n    41→**Status:** INVESTIGATING\n    42→**Incident Commander:** <user — ask if unknown>\n    43→\n    44→## Impact\n    45→\n    46→- **What broke:** <from description>\n    47→- **Who is affected:** <estimate — ask if unknown>\n    48→\n    49→## Timeline\n    50→\n    51→| Time (UTC) | Event |\n    52→|-----------|-------|\n    53→| HH:MM | Incident opened |\n    54→\n    55→## Root Cause\n    56→\n    57→(investigating)\n    58→\n    59→## Resolution\n    60→\n    61→(in progress)\n    62→\n    63→## Action Items\n    64→\n    65→| Action | Owner | Due | Ticket |\n    66→|--------|-------|-----|--------|\n    67→```\n    68→\n    69→### 4. Guide Root Cause Analysis\n    94→\n    95→Ask diagnostic questions based on the symptoms:\n    96→- \"When did it start? Was there a recent deploy?\"\n    97→- \"What do the error logs show? Specific accounts?)\"\n   100→\n   101→As answers come in, update the Timeline section in the incident doc.\n   102→\n   103→### 6. Resolution\n   104→\n   105→When the user says the issue is resolved:\n   106→\n   107→1. Update incident doc:\n   108→   - Add resolution time to timeline\n   109→   - Fill in Root Cause (best known so far)\n   110→   - Change Status to RESOLVED\n   111→   - Calculate duration\n   112→\n   113→2. Generate resolved status page message:\n   114→   ```\n   115→   🟢 Resolved — [Service] Operational\n   116→   The issue has been resolved.\n   117→   Duration: X hours Y minutes\n   118→   Post-mortem will follow within 48 hours.\n   119→   ```\n   120→\n   121→3. Prompt post-mortem:\n   122→   ```\n   123→   Incident closed. A post-mortem is recommended for P0/P1 incidents.\n   124→   Run: /incident post-mortem docs/incidents/<this-file>.md\n   125→   ```\n   126→\n   127→### 7. Post-Mortem Mode\n   128→\n   129→If `$ARGUMENTS` starts with `post-mortem`:\n   130→\n   131→Read the incident file. Generate a full post-mortem using the blameless format (see `incident-response` skill):\n   132→- Executive summary\n   133→- What went well / wrong\n   134→- 5 Whys root cause analysis\n   135→- Action items (P0/P1/P2 priorities)\n   136→\n   137→Save to `docs/incidents/post-mortems/YYYY-MM-DD-<name>-post-mortem.md`.\n   138→\n   139→### 8. Verify Clean State\n    12→\n    13→```bash\n    14→git status  # must be clean\n    15→git branch  # must be on main\n    16→git log --oneline -3\n    17→```\n    18→\n    19→If not clean or not on main, stop and report: \"Please commit or stash changes and switch to main before releasing.\"\n    20→\n    21→### 2. Show Plan — WAIT FOR CONFIRMATION\n    47→\n    48→```\n    49→RELEASE PLAN\n    50→════════════════════\n    51→\n    52→Current:  v1.3.2\n    53→New:      v1.4.0 (MINOR — new feature detected)\n    54→\n    55→Commits since v1.3.2:\n    56→  feat(auth): add OAuth2 GitHub login (#241)\n    57→  feat(api): add cursor-based pagination (#234)\n    58→  fix(auth): handle expired tokens (#243)\n    59→  fix(orders): race condition in processing (#245)\n    60→  docs: update API authentication guide\n    61→\n    62→CHANGELOG will add:\n    63→  ## [1.4.0] — 2026-03-06\n    64→  ### Added\n    65→    - OAuth2 GitHub login\n    66→    - Cursor-based pagination on list endpoints\n    67→  ### Fixed\n    68→    - Expired token handling\n    69→    - Race condition in order processing\n    70→\n    71→Files to update:\n    72→  CHANGELOG.md\n    73→  package.json (version field)\n    74→\n    75→Tag to create: v1.4.0\n    76→\n    77→Continue?     1→---\n     2→description: Orchestrate multiple agents for complex tasks — auto-selects coordination pattern (fan-out, split-role, explorer+validator, worktree, pipeline)\n     3→agent: orchestrator\n     4→subtask: true\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→# Orchestrate Command\n     8→\n     9→Orchestrate multiple specialized agents for: $ARGUMENTS\n    10→\n    11→## Pattern Auto-Selection\n    12→\n    13→Before creating the execution plan, analyze the task and select the best coordination pattern:\n    14→\n    15→| Task Signal | Pattern |\n    16→|-------------|---------|\n    17→| Review/analyze N files independently | **Fan-Out → Fan-In** |\n    18→| Decision needing multiple perspectives | **Split-Role** |\n    19→| Unknown codebase / research task | **Explorer + Validator** |\n    20→| Parallel independent features | **Worktree Isolation** |\n    21→| Feature from plan → test → code → review | **Sequential Pipeline** |\n    22→\n    23→Load skill `multi-agent-coordination` for full pattern specifications.\n    24→\n    25→## Your Task\n    26→\n    27→1. **Analyze the task** — identify complexity, dependencies, and domain\n    28→2. **Select pattern** — choose from the 5 patterns above and justify\n    29→3. **Identify optimal agents** — match agents to subtasks\n    30→4. **Create execution plan** — phases with dependencies\n    31→5. **Execute** — parallel where possible, sequential where required\n    32→6. **Detect conflicts** — compare agent outputs for contradictions at the same code locations\n    33→7. **Resolve conflicts** — apply the priority hierarchy from `docs/agent-priority-hierarchy.md`; every conflict must appear in `### Conflicts Resolved`\n    34→8. **Synthesize** — merge results into unified output\n    35→\n    36→## Available Agents\n    37→\n    38→| Agent | Specialty | Use For |\n    39→|-------|-----------|---------|\n    40→| planner | Implementation planning | Complex python-reviewer | Python | Python-specific review |\n    54→\n    55→## Coordination Patterns\n    56→\n    57→### Fan-Out / Fan-In\n    58→```\n    59→Orchestrator ─┬─ Agent A (target-1) ─┐\n    60→              ├─ Agent B (target-2) ─┼─ Synthesizer\n    61→              └─ Agent C (target-3) ─┘\n    62→```\n    63→Use: identical task across multiple independent targets\n    64→\n    65→### Split-Role\n    66→```\n    67→Orchestrator ─┬─ Implementer (build it)\n    68→              ├─ Critic (find issues)\n    69→              └─ Security (find vulns)\n    70→                       ↓ reconcile\n    71→```\n    72→Use: same task, different perspectives needed\n    73→\n    74→### Explorer + Validator\n    75→```\n    76→Phase 1: Explorer → findings\n    77→Phase 2: Validator → verified-findings\n    78→Phase 3: Implementer → uses verified-findings\n    79→```\n    80→Use: unknown codebase, uncertain requirements\n    81→\n    82→### Worktree Isolation\n    83→```\n    84→Orchestrator ─┬─ Agent A (isolation: worktree, feature/A)\n    85→              ├─ Agent B (isolation: worktree, feature/B)\n    86→              └─ Agent C (isolation: worktree, fix/C)\n    87→                       ↓ review + merge diffs\n    88→```\n    89→Use: parallel independent write operations\n    90→\n    91→### Sequential Pipeline\n    92→```\n    93→planner → tdd-guide → implementer 111→- Depends on: Phase 1\n   112→\n   113→### Phase N: Synthesis\n   114→- Combine results from Phase N-1\n   115→- Generate unified output\n   116→\n   117→## Coordination Rules\n   118→\n   119→1. **Pattern first** — select and justify pattern before planning\n   120→2. **Parallelize by default** — only serialize when there's a dependency\n   121→3. **Worktree for writes** — use `isolation: \"worktree\"` for any agent that modifies files\n   122→4. **Minimal context per agent** — pass only what the agent needs\n   123→5. **Synthesize explicitly** — always produce a unified final output\n hierarchy; never silently apply a lower-priority recommendation\n   126→\n   127→---\n   128→\n   129→**See also:** Skill `multi-agent-coordination` for full pattern specifications.\n   130→**Conflict Optionally opens a PR to upstream clarc.\"\n     3→---\n     4→\n     5→# Promote Skill Command\n     6→\n     7→Copies a project-local skill to global clarc scope, making it available across all projects.\n     8→\n     9→## Usage\n    10→\n    11→```\n    12→/promote-skill <name>\n    13→/promote-skill <name> --pr\n    14→```\n    15→\n    16→## What It Does\n    17→\n    18→1. Validates that `.clarc/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` exists\n    19→2. Warns if the skill contains project-specific content (checks for hardcoded paths, internal URLs, company names in the description)\n    20→3. Copies `.clarc/skills/<name>/` to `~/.clarc/skills/<name>/`\n    21→4. Updates `~/.clarc/skills/INDEX.md` with the new skill entry (if it exists)\n    22→5. If `--pr` is passed and `gh` is available: opens a pull request to the upstream clarc repository\n    23→\n    24→## Implementation Steps\n    25→\n    26→### 1. Locate the skill\n    27→\n    28→```bash\n    29→SKILL_DIR=\".clarc/skills/<name>\"\n    30→SKILL_FILE=\"$SKILL_DIR/SKILL.md\"\n    31→```\n    32→\n    33→If `$SKILL_FILE` does not exist → print error and stop.\n    34→\n    35→### 2. Warn about project-specific content\n    36→\n    37→Read the SKILL.md and flag if it contains:\n    38→- Absolute paths (e.g., `/Users/`, `/home/`)\n    39→- Internal URLs (`.internal`, `.corp`, company-specific domains)\n    40→- Words suggesting PII or secrets\n    41→\n    42→Print a warning per item, then ask the user to confirm before continuing.\n    43→\n    44→### 3. Copy to global scope\n    45→\n    46→```bash\n    47→cp -r \".clarc/skills/<name>\" \"$HOME/.clarc/skills/<name>\"\n    48→```\n    49→\n    50→If `~/.clarc/skills/<name>` already exists, ask before overwriting.\n    51→\n    52→### 4. Update INDEX.md (if present)\n    53→\n    54→Add a row to `~/.clarc/skills/INDEX.md`:\n    55→\n    56→```\n    57→| <name> | <title> | <description> |\n    58→```\n    59→\n    60→### 5. Open PR (--pr flag)\n    61→\n    62→If `--pr` is passed and `gh` is installed:\n    63→\n    64→```bash\n    65→cd ~/.clarc\n    66→git checkout -b feat/add-skill-<name>\n    67→git add skills/<name>/\n    68→git commit -m \"feat: add <name> skill (promoted from project)\"\n    69→gh pr create --title \"feat: add <name> skill\" --body \"Promoted from project-local scope.\\n\\n<description>\"\n    70→```\n    71→\n    72→## Example Output\n    73→\n    74→```\n    75→/promote-skill our-auth-pattern\n    76→\n    77→Promoting: our-auth-pattern\n    78→Source:    .clarc/skills/our-auth-pattern/SKILL.md\n    79→Target:    ~/.clarc/skills/our-auth-pattern/\n    80→\n    81→⚠️  Warning: SKILL.md contains internal URL: auth.internal.corp\n    82→   → Review and remove project-specific content before promoting.\n    83→\n    84→Proceed? [y/N]: y\n    85→\n    86→✅ Promoted to ~/.clarc/skills/our-auth-pattern/\n    87→   Skill is now available globally across all projects.\n    88→\n    89→To propose this skill to all clarc users:\n    90→   /promote-skill our-auth-pattern --pr\n    91→```\n    92→\n    93→## Safety Notes\n    94→\n    95→- **Never** auto-promote without user confirmation\n    96→- **Always** warn about project-specific content\n    97→- Promoted skills are global — remove company names, internal URLs, PII\n    98→- The original `.clarc/skills/<name>/` is **not** deleted after promotion\n    99→\n   100→## Related\n   101→\n   102→- Command: `/skill-create --local <name>` — scaffold a new project-local skill\n   103→- Command: `/skills-local` — list all project-local skills\n   104→- Skill: `project-local-skills` — full workflow guide\n   105→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Produces user stories, acceptance criteria, story point estimates, and a prioritized task list ready to paste into Jira, Linear, or GitHub Issues.\n     3→---\n     4→\n     5→# Breakdown — Feature to Sprint Tasks\n     6→\n     7→Break down: $ARGUMENTS\n     8→\n     9→---\n    10→\n    11→## Step 1 — Clarify scope\n    12→\n    13→From $ARGUMENTS, identify:\n    14→- **What** is being built (user-facing feature or technical work?)\n    15→- **Who** is the user (persona, role)?\n    16→- **Why** does it matter (business value, pain point solved)?\n    17→- **What is out of scope** (explicitly name 2-3 things not included)?\n    18→\n    19→If scope is unclear, ask before proceeding.\n    20→\n    21→## Step 2 — Write the epic\n    22→\n    23→```\n    24→As a [persona],\n    25→I want [capability],\n    26→So that [outcome/value].\n    27→\n    28→Acceptance criteria (epic-level):\n    29→- [ ] [Criterion 1]\n    30→- [ ] [Criterion 2]\n    31→- [ ] [Criterion 3]\n    32→```\n    33→\n    34→## Step 3 — Identify task types\n    35→\n    36→Categorize work into:\n    37→- **Frontend** — UI components, pages, interactions\n    38→- **Backend** — API endpoints, business logic, data models\n    39→- **Infrastructure** — deployment, configuration, migrations\n    40→- **Testing** — unit, integration, E2E tests\n    41→- **Design** — wireframes, specs (if needed)\n    42→- **Documentation** — internal docs, changelog\n    43→\n    44→## Step 4 — Write user stories\n    45→\n    46→For each meaningful unit of deliverable value, write a story:\n    47→\n    48→```\n    49→[SHORT TITLE] (N points)\n    50→\n    51→As a [user type],\n    52→I want [specific action or capability],\n    53→So that [specific outcome].\n    54→\n    55→Acceptance criteria:\n    56→- [ ] [Specific, testable criterion]\n    57→- [ ] [Edge case handled]\n    58→- [ ] [Error state handled]\n    59→\n    60→Technical notes:\n    61→- [Implementation hint, API endpoint, component name]\n    62→```\n    63→\n    64→Story point guidelines:\n    65→- **1 pt** — trivial change, < 2 hours\n    66→- **2 pt** — small, well-understood, < half day\n    67→- **3 pt** — medium complexity, 1 day\n    68→- **5 pt** — complex or cross-cutting, 2-3 days\n    69→- **8 pt** — large, should be broken down further\n    70→- **13+ pt** — must split into smaller stories\n    71→\n    72→## Step 5 — Sequence and prioritize\n    73→\n    74→Order stories by:\n    75→1. **Blockers first** — infrastructure, migrations, foundational APIs\n    76→2. **Happy path** — core user journey (minimum lovable product)\n    77→3. **Error states** — validation, edge cases, empty states\n    78→4. **Polish** — loading states, animations, accessibility\n    79→5. **Nice-to-have** — additional features, optimizations\n    80→\n    81→## Step 6 — Output\n    82→\n    83→Produce the sprint task list:\n    84→\n    85→```markdown\n    86→## Epic: [Title]\n    87→\n    88→**Persona**: [User type]\n    89→**Goal**: [One sentence]\n    90→**Out of scope**: [2-3 items]\n    91→**Total estimate**: [N points]\n    92→\n    93→---\n    94→\n    95→### Sprint Tasks (prioritized)\n    96→\n    97→#### P0 — Blockers\n    98→- [ ] [TASK-001] [Title] (N pts) — [one-line description]\n    99→\n   100→#### P1 — Core flow\n   101→- [ ] [TASK-002] [Title] (N pts)\n   102→- [ ] [TASK-003] [Title] (N pts)\n   103→\n   104→#### P2 — Error handling\n   105→- [ ] [TASK-004] [Title] (N pts)\n   106→\n   107→#### P3 — Polish\n   108→- [ ] [TASK-005] [Title] (N pts)\n   109→\n   110→---\n   111→\n   112→### Dependencies\n   113→- [Task X] must complete before [Task Y]\n   114→- External: [any external dependency]\n   115→\n   116→### Definition of Done\n   117→- [ ] All acceptance criteria met\n   118→- [ ] Unit tests written and passing\n   119→- [ ] PR reviewed and merged\n   120→- [ ] Deployed to staging and smoke tested\n   121→- [ ] Product/design sign-off\n  → Keep local (higher confidence)\n    67→\n    68→  ⚠️ test-first-workflow\n    69→     Local: 0.75 confidence\n    70→     Import: 0.9 confidence\n    71→     → Update to import (higher Run the coverage command\n    23→2. Parse the output (JSON summary or terminal output)\n    24→3. List files **below 80% coverage**, sorted worst-first\n    25→4. For each under-covered file, identify:\n    26→   - Untested functions or methods\n    27→   - Missing branch coverage (if/else, switch, error paths)\n    28→   - Dead code that inflates the denominator\n    29→\n    30→## Step 3: Generate Missing Tests\n    31→\n    32→For each under-covered file, generate tests following this priority:\n    33→\n    34→1. **Happy path** — Core functionality with valid inputs\n    35→2. **Error handling** — Invalid inputs, missing data, network failures\n    36→3. **Edge cases** — Empty arrays, null/undefined, boundary values (0, -1, MAX_INT)\n    37→4. **Branch coverage** — Each if/else, switch case, ternary\n    38→\n    39→### Test Generation Rules\n    40→\n    41→- Place tests adjacent to source: `foo.ts` → `foo.test.ts` (or project convention)\n    42→- Use existing test patterns from the project (import style, assertion library, mocking approach)\n    43→- Mock external dependencies (database, APIs, file system)\n    44→- Each test should be independent — no shared mutable state between tests\n    45→- Name tests descriptively: `test_create_user_with_duplicate_email_returns_409`\n    46→\n    47→## Step 4: Verify\n    48→\n    49→1. Run the full test suite — all tests must pass\n    50→2. Re-run coverage — verify improvement\n    51→3. If still below 80%, repeat Step 3 for remaining gaps\n    52→\n    53→## Step 5: Report\n    54→\n    55→Show before/after comparison:\n    56→\n    57→```\n    58→Coverage Report\n    59→──────────────────────────────\n    60→File                   Before  After\n    61→src/services/auth.ts   45%     88%\n    62→src/utils/validation.ts 32%    82%\n    63→──────────────────────────────\n    64→Overall:               67%     84%  ✅\n    65→```\n    66→\n    67→## Focus Areas\n    68→\n    69→- Functions with complex branching (high cyclomatic complexity)\n    70→- Error handlers and catch blocks\n    71→- Utility functions used across the codebase\n    72→- API endpoint handlers (request → response flow)\n    73→- Edge cases: null, undefined, empty string, empty array, zero, negative numbers\n    74→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Read `~/.clarc/checkpoints.log` — find the most recent checkpoint entry\n    18→2. Check for uncommitted changes that would be lost:\n    19→   - If dirty working tree: warn the user before proceeding\n    20→3. Determine strategy from the log entry:\n    21→   - `strategy: \"stash\"` → run `git stash pop`\n    22→   - `strategy: \"commit\"` → run `git reset HEAD~1`\n    23→4. Show which files were restored\n    24→5. Remove the log entry (or ask user if they want to keep it)\n    25→\n    26→## Safety Checks\n    27→\n    28→- **No checkpoints**: show \"No checkpoints found. Nothing to undo.\"\n    29→- **Dirty working tree**: warn \"You have uncommitted changes. Undo may cause conflicts. Continue? [y/N]\"\n    30→- **Wrong directory**: if `cwd` in log doesn't match current dir, warn the user\n    31→\n    32→## Implementation\n    33→\n    34→```bash\n    35→# Read last checkpoint\n    36→LAST=$(cat ~/.clarc/checkpoints.log | node -e \"\n    37→const d=JSON.parse(require('fs').readFileSync('/dev/stdin','utf8'));\n    38→const last=d[d.length-1];\n    39→if(!last){console.error('No checkpoints found.');process.exit(1);}\n    40→console.log(JSON.stringify(last));\n    41→\")\n    42→\n    43→# Extract strategy\n    44→STRATEGY=$(echo $LAST | node -e \"process.stdout.write(JSON.parse(require('fs').readFileSync('/dev/stdin','utf8')).strategy)\")\n    45→\n    46→if [ \"$STRATEGY\" = \"stash\" ]; then\n    47→  git stash pop\n    48→elif [ \"$STRATEGY\" = \"commit\" ]; then\n    49→  git reset HEAD~1\n    50→fi\n    51→```\n    52→\n    53→## Usage Example\n    54→\n    55→```\n    56→User: /undo\n    57→Claude: Last checkpoint: 2026-03-08T14:23:11Z (commit abc1234)\n    58→        Files restored: src/api/users.ts, src/api/auth.ts\n    59→        Undo complete. Working tree restored to state before last Edit.\n    60→```\n    61→\n    62→## Related\n    63→\n    64→- `scripts/hooks/auto-checkpoint.js` — creates checkpoints automatically\n    65→- `~/.clarc/checkpoints.log` — checkpoint history (JSON array, max 50 entries)\n    66→- `/session-cost` — view session cost estimates\n    67→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. A user expecting TDD enforcement from `/python-test` will be disappointed. | Either: (a) update `python-test` to enforce TDD (matching `go-test` and `rust-test`), or (b) rename `go-test` to `go-tdd` and `rust-test` to `rust-tdd` to distinguish methodology from execution. Next steps section tells the user exactly what to do after the release. |\n| 3 | `/evaluate` | Clear argument contract with three distinct cases: exact name, partial match, and empty (interactive list).
